WindowAssigner Base Class\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/WindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nThe abstract base class `WindowAssigner<T, W extends Window>` is the primary extension point for implementing custom window assignment logic. Developers must implement the following abstract methods:\\n\\n- **`Collection<W> assignWindows(T element, long timestamp, WindowAssignerContext context)`** — Assigns zero or more windows to each incoming element based on the element, its timestamp, and the current processing time context.\\n- **`Trigger<T, W> getDefaultTrigger()`** — Returns the default trigger for this window assigner (e.g., EventTimeTrigger for event-time windows).\\n- **`TypeSerializer<W> getWindowSerializer(ExecutionConfig executionConfig)`** — Provides serialization support for the window type.\\n- **`boolean isEventTime()`** — Indicates whether windows are based on event time (true) or processing time (false).\\n\\nThe class also defines an inner `WindowAssignerContext` interface with a single method `getCurrentProcessingTime()` to support assigners that need wall-clock time.\\n\\n### 2. MergingWindowAssigner Subclass\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/MergingWindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nThis abstract class extends `WindowAssigner<T, W extends Window>` and adds support for session-style window merging, required when windows can overlap and need to be combined. Key method:\\n\\n- **`void mergeWindows(Collection<W> windows, MergeCallback<W> callback)`** — Determines which windows should be merged. Implementations iterate over window candidates and call `callback.merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)` to signal merge operations. The callback includes an inner interface `MergeCallback<W>` with a single method `merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)`.\\n\\n### 3. Trigger Base Class\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/triggers/Trigger.java`\\n\\nThe abstract base class `Trigger<T, W extends Window>` defines the lifecycle for window evaluation. Developers must implement:\\n\\n- **`TriggerResult onElement(T element, long timestamp, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when an element arrives. Returns a TriggerResult indicating whether to fire, purge, or continue the window.\\n- **`TriggerResult onEventTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when an event-time timer fires (watermark crosses registered time).\\n- **`TriggerResult onProcessingTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when a processing-time timer fires (wall-clock time passes registered time).\\n- **`void clear(W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Clears all state for the window, including registered timers.\\n\\nFor session windows, implement additionally:\\n- **`boolean canMerge()`** — Returns true to indicate this trigger supports merging (overrides default false).\\n- **`void onMerge(W window, OnMergeContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when windows are merged; must merge any trigger state using the provided `OnMergeContext` interface.\\n\\nThe `TriggerContext` interface provides access to state, timers, metrics, and watermark/processing-time information. The `OnMergeContext` extends `TriggerContext` to support `mergePartitionedState(StateDescriptor<S, ?> stateDescriptor)` for merging trigger state.\\n\\n### 4. EventTimeSessionWindows Reference Implementation\\n**Location:** `flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/EventTimeSessionWindows.java`\\n\\nThis concrete implementation demonstrates the pattern:\\n- **Class Declaration:** `public class EventTimeSessionWindows extends MergingWindowAssigner<Object, TimeWindow>`\\n- **`assignWindows()` implementation:** Returns `Collections.singletonList(new TimeWindow(timestamp, timestamp + sessionTimeout))` — creates a single window from the element timestamp to timestamp + session timeout.\\n- **`mergeWindows()` implementation:** Delegates to `TimeWindow.mergeWindows(windows, c)` — reuses utility logic to merge overlapping TimeWindows.\\n- **Additional methods:** \\n  - `getDefaultTrigger()` returns `EventTimeTrigger.create()`\\n  - `isEventTime()` returns `true`\\n  - Factory method `withGap(Duration size)` creates instances with a session timeout\\n\\n### 5. TimeWindow Class\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/windows/TimeWindow.java`\\n\\nThis class represents time-interval windows. Key features:\\n- **Constructor:** `TimeWindow(long start, long end)` — creates a window [start, end), where start is inclusive and end is exclusive.\\n- **Accessors:** `getStart()`, `getEnd()`, `maxTimestamp()` (returns end - 1)\\n- **Utilities:** \\n  - `intersects(TimeWindow other)` — tests overlap\\n  - `cover(TimeWindow other)` — computes minimal covering window\\n  - Static helper `mergeWindows(Collection<TimeWindow> windows, MergeCallback<TimeWindow> c)` — sorts windows by start time and merges all overlapping windows, calling the callback for each merge operation.\\n- **Serialization:** Includes an inner `Serializer` class for type serialization support.\\n\\n### Integration Flow\\nA custom window assigner implementation follows this pattern:\\n1. Extend `WindowAssigner` (or `MergingWindowAssigner` for session windows)\\n2. Implement `assignWindows()` to produce window objects (typically TimeWindow instances)\\n3. Return an appropriate `Trigger` subclass from `getDefaultTrigger()` (e.g., EventTimeTrigger)\\n4. Provide a `TypeSerializer` for your window type\\n5. If merging windows, extend `MergingWindowAssigner` and implement `mergeWindows()` to determine which windows overlap and should be combined\\n6. If using a merging assigner, ensure the trigger's `canMerge()` returns true and `onMerge()` is properly implemented\\n\\nThe EventTimeSessionWindows class exemplifies this design: it assigns windows based on gaps in event time, delegates merging logic to TimeWindow utilities, and integrates with EventTimeTrigger for watermark-based window firing.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5239,"cache_read_input_tokens":76465,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5239},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"bacb8035-f123-4def-8b3e-7da15526b1fc","uuid":"244a4439-555e-4350-be0f-2a2d7c5cc23a"}

Developers must implement the following abstract methods:\\n\\n- **`Collection<W> assignWindows(T element, long timestamp, WindowAssignerContext context)`** — Assigns zero or more windows to each incoming element based on the element, its timestamp, and the current processing time context.\\n- **`Trigger<T, W> getDefaultTrigger()`** — Returns the default trigger for this window assigner (e.g., EventTimeTrigger for event-time windows).\\n- **`TypeSerializer<W> getWindowSerializer(ExecutionConfig executionConfig)`** — Provides serialization support for the window type.\\n- **`boolean isEventTime()`** — Indicates whether windows are based on event time (true) or processing time (false).\\n\\nThe class also defines an inner `WindowAssignerContext` interface with a single method `getCurrentProcessingTime()` to support assigners that need wall-clock time.\\n\\n### 2. Key method:\\n\\n- **`void mergeWindows(Collection<W> windows, MergeCallback<W> callback)`** — Determines which windows should be merged. Implementations iterate over window candidates and call `callback.merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)` to signal merge operations. The callback includes an inner interface `MergeCallback<W>` with a single method `merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)`.\\n\\n### 3. Trigger Base Class\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/triggers/Trigger.java`\\n\\nThe abstract base class `Trigger<T, W extends Window>` defines the lifecycle for window evaluation. Developers must implement:\\n\\n- **`TriggerResult onElement(T element, long timestamp, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when an element arrives. Returns a TriggerResult indicating whether to fire, purge, or continue the window.\\n- **`TriggerResult onEventTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when an event-time timer fires (watermark crosses registered time).\\n- **`TriggerResult onProcessingTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when a processing-time timer fires (wall-clock time passes registered time).\\n- **`void clear(W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Clears all state for the window, including registered timers.\\n\\nFor session windows, implement additionally:\\n- **`boolean canMerge()`** — Returns true to indicate this trigger supports merging (overrides default false).\\n- **`void onMerge(W window, OnMergeContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when windows are merged; must merge any trigger state using the provided `OnMergeContext` interface.\\n\\nThe `TriggerContext` interface provides access to state, timers, metrics, and watermark/processing-time information. The `OnMergeContext` extends `TriggerContext` to support `mergePartitionedState(StateDescriptor<S, ?> stateDescriptor)` for merging trigger state.\\n\\n### 4. WindowAssigner Base Class\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/WindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nThe abstract base class `WindowAssigner<T, W extends Window>` is the primary extension point for implementing custom window assignment logic. Developers must implement the following abstract methods:\\n\\n- **`Collection<W> assignWindows(T element, long timestamp, WindowAssignerContext context)`** — Assigns zero or more windows to each incoming element based on the element, its timestamp, and the current processing time context.\\n- **`Trigger<T, W> getDefaultTrigger()`** — Returns the default trigger for this window assigner (e.g., EventTimeTrigger for event-time windows).\\n- **`TypeSerializer<W> getWindowSerializer(ExecutionConfig executionConfig)`** — Provides serialization support for the window type.\\n- **`boolean isEventTime()`** — Indicates whether windows are based on event time (true) or processing time (false).\\n\\nThe class also defines an inner `WindowAssignerContext` interface with a single method `getCurrentProcessingTime()` to support assigners that need wall-clock time.\\n\\n### 2. MergingWindowAssigner Subclass\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/MergingWindowAssigner.java`\\n\\nThis abstract class extends `WindowAssigner<T, W extends Window>` and adds support for session-style window merging, required when windows can overlap and need to be combined. Key method:\\n\\n- **`void mergeWindows(Collection<W> windows, MergeCallback<W> callback)`** — Determines which windows should be merged. Implementations iterate over window candidates and call `callback.merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)` to signal merge operations. The callback includes an inner interface `MergeCallback<W>` with a single method `merge(Collection<W> toBeMerged, W mergeResult)`.\\n\\n### 3. Trigger Base Class\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/triggers/Trigger.java`\\n\\nThe abstract base class `Trigger<T, W extends Window>` defines the lifecycle for window evaluation. Developers must implement:\\n\\n- **`TriggerResult onElement(T element, long timestamp, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when an element arrives. Returns a TriggerResult indicating whether to fire, purge, or continue the window.\\n- **`TriggerResult onEventTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when an event-time timer fires (watermark crosses registered time).\\n- **`TriggerResult onProcessingTime(long time, W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when a processing-time timer fires (wall-clock time passes registered time).\\n- **`void clear(W window, TriggerContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Clears all state for the window, including registered timers.\\n\\nFor session windows, implement additionally:\\n- **`boolean canMerge()`** — Returns true to indicate this trigger supports merging (overrides default false).\\n- **`void onMerge(W window, OnMergeContext ctx) throws Exception`** — Called when windows are merged; must merge any trigger state using the provided `OnMergeContext` interface.\\n\\nThe `TriggerContext` interface provides access to state, timers, metrics, and watermark/processing-time information. The `OnMergeContext` extends `TriggerContext` to support `mergePartitionedState(StateDescriptor<S, ?> stateDescriptor)` for merging trigger state.\\n\\n### 4. EventTimeSessionWindows Reference Implementation\\n**Location:** `flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/assigners/EventTimeSessionWindows.java`\\n\\nThis concrete implementation demonstrates the pattern:\\n- **Class Declaration:** `public class EventTimeSessionWindows extends MergingWindowAssigner<Object, TimeWindow>`\\n- **`assignWindows()` implementation:** Returns `Collections.singletonList(new TimeWindow(timestamp, timestamp + sessionTimeout))` — creates a single window from the element timestamp to timestamp + session timeout.\\n- **`mergeWindows()` implementation:** Delegates to `TimeWindow.mergeWindows(windows, c)` — reuses utility logic to merge overlapping TimeWindows.\\n- **Additional methods:** \\n  - `getDefaultTrigger()` returns `EventTimeTrigger.create()`\\n  - `isEventTime()` returns `true`\\n  - Factory method `withGap(Duration size)` creates instances with a session timeout\\n\\n### 5. TimeWindow Class\\n**Location:** `flink-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/streaming/api/windowing/windows/TimeWindow.java`\\n\\nThis class represents time-interval windows. Key features:\\n- **Constructor:** `TimeWindow(long start, long end)` — creates a window [start, end), where start is inclusive and end is exclusive.\\n- **Accessors:** `getStart()`, `getEnd()`, `maxTimestamp()` (returns end - 1)\\n- **Utilities:** \\n  - `intersects(TimeWindow other)` — tests overlap\\n  - `cover(TimeWindow other)` — computes minimal covering window\\n  - Static helper `mergeWindows(Collection<TimeWindow> windows, MergeCallback<TimeWindow> c)` — sorts windows by start time and merges all overlapping windows, calling the callback for each merge operation.\\n- **Serialization:** Includes an inner `Serializer` class for type serialization support.\\n\\n### Integration Flow\\nA custom window assigner implementation follows this pattern:\\n1. Extend `WindowAssigner` (or `MergingWindowAssigner` for session windows)\\n2. Implement `assignWindows()` to produce window objects (typically TimeWindow instances)\\n3. Return an appropriate `Trigger` subclass from `getDefaultTrigger()` (e.g., EventTimeTrigger)\\n4. Provide a `TypeSerializer` for your window type\\n5. If merging windows, extend `MergingWindowAssigner` and implement `mergeWindows()` to determine which windows overlap and should be combined\\n6. If using a merging assigner, ensure the trigger's `canMerge()` returns true and `onMerge()` is properly implemented\\n\\nThe EventTimeSessionWindows class exemplifies this design: it assigns windows based on gaps in event time, delegates merging logic to TimeWindow utilities, and integrates with EventTimeTrigger for watermark-based window firing.\"\n}\n","numLines":98,"startLine":1,"totalLines":98}}}
